 <tr>\n        <th scope="row">\n         <a href="/wiki/Specialty_(medicine)" title="Specialty (medicine)">\n          Specialty\n         </a>\n        </th>\n        <td>\n         <a href="/wiki/Rheumatology" title="Rheumatology">\n          Rheumatology\n         </a>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <th scope="row">\n         Symptoms\n        </th>\n        <td>\n         Increased risk of a\n         <a href="/wiki/Bone_fracture" title="Bone fracture">\n          broken bone\n         </a>\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NIH2014_3-0">\n          <a href="#cite_note-NIH2014-3">\n           [3]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <th scope="row">\n         <a href="/wiki/Complication_(medicine)" title="Complication (medicine)">\n          Complications\n         </a>\n        </th>\n        <td>\n         <a href="/wiki/Chronic_pain" title="Chronic pain">\n          Chronic pain\n         </a>\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NIH2014_3-1">\n          <a href="#cite_note-NIH2014-3">\n           [3]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <th scope="row">\n         Usual onset\n        </th>\n        <td>\n         Older age\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NIH2014_3-2">\n          <a href="#cite_note-NIH2014-3">\n           [3]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <th scope="row">\n         <a href="/wiki/Risk_factor" title="Risk factor">\n          Risk factors\n         </a>\n        </th>\n        <td>\n         <a href="/wiki/Alcoholism" title="Alcoholism">\n          Alcoholism\n         </a>\n         ,\n         <a href="/wiki/Anorexia_nervosa" title="Anorexia nervosa">\n          anorexia\n         </a>\n         ,\n         <a href="/wiki/Hyperthyroidism" title="Hyperthyroidism">\n          hyperthyroidism\n         </a>\n         ,\n         <a href="/wiki/Gastrointestinal_disease" title="Gastrointestinal disease">\n          gastrointestinal diseases\n         </a>\n         ,\n         <a href="/wiki/Oophorectomy" title="Oophorectomy">\n          surgical removal of the ovaries\n         </a>\n         ,\n         <a href="/wiki/Kidney_disease" title="Kidney disease">\n          kidney disease\n         </a>\n         , smoking, certain medication\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NIH2014_3-3">\n          <a href="#cite_note-NIH2014-3">\n           [3]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <th scope="row">\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Diagnostic_method" title="Diagnostic method">\n          Diagnostic method\n         </a>\n        </th>\n        <td>\n         <a href="/wiki/Dual-energy_X-ray_absorptiometry" title="Dual-energy X-ray absorptiometry">\n          Dual-energy X-ray absorptiometry\n         </a>\n         at the hip\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHOcriteria_4-0">\n          <a href="#cite_note-WHOcriteria-4">\n           [4]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <th scope="row">\n         Treatment\n        </th>\n        <td>\n         Good diet, exercise,\n         <a href="/wiki/Fall_prevention" title="Fall prevention">\n          fall prevention\n         </a>\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NIH2014_3-4">\n          <a href="#cite_note-NIH2014-3">\n           [3]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <th scope="row">\n         Medication\n        </th>\n        <td>\n         <a href="/wiki/Bisphosphonate" title="Bisphosphonate">\n          Bisphosphonates\n         </a>\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wells2008_5-0">\n          <a href="#cite_note-Wells2008-5">\n           [5]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wells2008a_6-0">\n          <a href="#cite_note-Wells2008a-6">\n           [6]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <th scope="row">\n         Frequency\n        </th>\n        <td>\n         15% (50s year olds), 70% (over 80 years)\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHOEpi_7-0">\n          <a href="#cite_note-WHOEpi-7">\n           [7]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr class="noprint">\n        <td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n         <div style="text-align: right;">\n          [\n          <a class="extiw" href="https://www.wikidata.org/wiki/Q165328" title="d:Q165328">\n           edit on Wikidata\n          </a>\n          ]\n         </div>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <p>\n       <b>\n        Osteoporosis\n       </b>\n       is a\n       <a href="/wiki/Disease" title="Disease">\n        disease\n       </a>\n       where increased bone weakness increases the risk of a\n       <a href="/wiki/Bone_fracture" title="Bone fracture">\n        broken bone\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NIH2014_3-5">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NIH2014-3">\n         [3]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       It is the most common reason for a broken bone among\n       <a href="/wiki/Old_age" title="Old age">\n        the elderly\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NIH2014_3-6">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NIH2014-3">\n         [3]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Bones that commonly break include the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vertebrae" title="Vertebrae">\n        vertebrae\n       </a>\n       in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Vertebral_column" title="Vertebral column">\n        spine\n       </a>\n       , the bones of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Forearm" title="Forearm">\n        forearm\n       </a>\n       , and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Hip" title="Hip">\n        hip\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gol2015_8-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Gol2015-8">\n         [8]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Until a broken bone occurs there are typically no symptoms.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NIH2014_3-7">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NIH2014-3">\n         [3]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Bones may weaken to such a degree that a break may occur with minor stress or spontaneously.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NIH2014_3-8">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NIH2014-3">\n         [3]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Chronic_pain" title="Chronic pain">\n        Chronic pain\n       </a>\n       and a decreased ability to carry out normal activities may occur following a broken bone.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NIH2014_3-9">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NIH2014-3">\n         [3]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Osteoporosis may be due to lower than normal\n       <a href="/wiki/Peak_bone_mass" title="Peak bone mass">\n        bone mass\n       </a>\n       and greater than normal bone loss.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NIH2014_3-10">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NIH2014-3">\n         [3]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Bone loss increases after\n       <a href="/wiki/Menopause" title="Menopause">\n        menopause\n       </a>\n       due to lower levels of\n       <a href="/wiki/Estrogen" title="Estrogen">\n        estrogen\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NIH2014_3-11">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NIH2014-3">\n         [3]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Osteoporosis may also occur due to a number of diseases or treatments including\n       <a href="/wiki/Alcoholism" title="Alcoholism">\n        alcoholism\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Anorexia_nervosa" title="Anorexia nervosa">\n        anorexia\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Hyperthyroidism" title="Hyperthyroidism">\n        hyperthyroidism\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Kidney_disease" title="Kidney disease">\n        kidney disease\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Oophorectomy" title="Oophorectomy">\n        surgical removal of the ovaries\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NIH2014_3-12">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NIH2014-3">\n         [3]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Certain medications increase the rate of bone loss including some\n       <a href="/wiki/Anticonvulsant" title="Anticonvulsant">\n        antiseizure medications\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Chemotherapy" title="Chemotherapy">\n        chemotherapy\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Proton_pump_inhibitor" title="Proton pump inhibitor">\n        proton pump inhibitors\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Selective_serotonin_reuptake_inhibitors" title="Selective serotonin reuptake inhibitors">\n        selective serotonin reuptake inhibitors\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Glucocorticoid" title="Glucocorticoid">\n        glucocorticosteroids\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NIH2014_3-13">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NIH2014-3">\n         [3]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Not enough exercise and smoking are also risk factors.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NIH2014_3-14">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NIH2014-3">\n         [3]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Osteoporosis is defined as a\n       <a href="/wiki/Bone_density" title="Bone density">\n        bone density\n       </a>\n       of 2.5\n       <a href="/wiki/Standard_deviation" title="Standard deviation">\n        standard deviations\n       </a>\n       below that of a young adult.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHOcriteria_4-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-WHOcriteria-4">\n         [4]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       This is typically measured by\n       <a href="/wiki/Dual-energy_X-ray_absorptiometry" title="Dual-energy X-ray absorptiometry">\n        dual-energy X-ray absorptiometry\n       </a>\n       at the hip.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHOcriteria_4-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-WHOcriteria-4">\n         [4]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Prevention of osteoporosis includes a proper diet during childhood and efforts to avoid medications that cause the condition.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NIH2014_3-15">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NIH2014-3">\n         [3]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Efforts to prevent broken bones in those with osteoporosis include a good diet, exercise, and\n       <a href="/wiki/Fall_prevention" title="Fall prevention">\n        fall prevention\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NIH2014_3-16">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NIH2014-3">\n         [3]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Lifestyle changes such as stopping smoking and not drinking alcohol may help.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NIH2014_3-17">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NIH2014-3">\n         [3]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Bisphosphonate" title="Bisphosphonate">\n        Biphosphonate medications\n       </a>\n       are useful in those with previous broken bones due to osteoporosis.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wells2008_5-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Wells2008-5">\n         [5]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wells2008a_6-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Wells2008a-6">\n         [6]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In those with osteoporosis but no previous broken bones they are less effective.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wells2008_5-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Wells2008-5">\n         [5]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wells2008a_6-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Wells2008a-6">\n         [6]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wells2008b_9-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Wells2008b-9">\n         [9]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       A number of other medications may also be useful.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NIH2014_3-18">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NIH2014-3">\n         [3]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10">\n        <a href="#cite_note-10">\n         [10]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Osteoporosis becomes more common with age.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NIH2014_3-19">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NIH2014-3">\n         [3]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       About 15% of\n       <a href="/wiki/White_people" title="White people">\n        white people\n       </a>\n       in their 50s and 70% of those over 80 are affected.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHOEpi_7-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-WHOEpi-7">\n         [7]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       It is more common in women than men.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NIH2014_3-20">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NIH2014-3">\n         [3]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Developed_world" title="Developed world">\n        developed world\n       </a>\n       , depending on the method of diagnosis, 2% to 8% of males and 9% to 38% of females are affected.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wade2014_11-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Wade2014-11">\n         [11]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Rates of disease in the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Developing_world" title="Developing world">\n        developing world\n       </a>\n       are unclear.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Han2008_12-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Han2008-12">\n         [12]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       About 22 million women and 5.5 million men in the\n       <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">\n        European Union\n       </a>\n       had osteoporosis in 2010.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sve2013_13-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Sve2013-13">\n         [13]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In the United States in 2010 about eight million women and one to two million men had osteoporosis.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wade2014_11-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Wade2014-11">\n         [11]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Will2015_14-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Will2015-14">\n         [14]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       White and\n       <a href="/wiki/Asian_people" title="Asian people">\n        Asian people\n       </a>\n       are at greater risk.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NIH2014_3-21">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NIH2014-3">\n         [3]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The word osteoporosis is from the Greek terms for "porous bones".\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">\n        <a href="#cite_note-15">\n         [15]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n      </p>\n      <div class="toc" id="toc">\n       <div class="toctitle">\n        <h2>\n         Contents\n        </h2>\n       </div>\n       <ul>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1">\n         <a href="#Signs_and_symptoms">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           1\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Signs and symptoms\n          </span>\n         </a>\n         <ul>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-2">\n           <a href="#Fractures">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             1.1\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Fractures\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-3">\n           <a href="#Falls_risk">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             1.2\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Falls risk\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n         </ul>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-4">\n         <a href="#Risk_factors">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           2\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Risk factors\n          </span>\n         </a>\n         <ul>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-5">\n           <a href="#Nonmodifiable">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             2.1\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Nonmodifiable\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-6">\n           <a href="#Potentially_modifiable">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             2.2\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Potentially modifiable\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-7">\n           <a href="#Medical_disorders">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             2.3\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Medical disorders\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-8">\n           <a href="#Medication">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             2.4\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Medication\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-9">\n           <a href="#Evolutionary">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             2.5\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Evolutionary\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n         </ul>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-10">\n         <a href="#Pathogenesis">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           3\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Pathogenesis\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-11">\n         <a href="#Diagnosis">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           4\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Diagnosis\n          </span>\n         </a>\n         <ul>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-12">\n           <a href="#Conventional_radiography">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             4.1\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Conventional radiography\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-13">\n           <a href="#Dual-energy_X-ray">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             4.2\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Dual-energy X-ray\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-14">\n           <a href="#Biomarkers">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             4.3\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Biomarkers\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-15">\n           <a href="#Other_measuring_tools">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             4.4\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Other measuring tools\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-16">\n           <a href="#Screening">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             4.5\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Screening\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n         </ul>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-17">\n         <a href="#Prevention">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           5\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Prevention\n          </span>\n         </a>\n         <ul>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-18">\n           <a href="#Nutrition">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             5.1\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Nutrition\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-19">\n           <a href="#Physical_exercise">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             5.2\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Physical exercise\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n         </ul>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-20">\n         <a href="#Management">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           6\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Management\n          </span>\n         </a>\n         <ul>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-21">\n           <a href="#Lifestyle">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             6.1\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Lifestyle\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-22">\n           <a href="#Medications">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             6.2\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Medications\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n         </ul>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-23">\n         <a href="#Prognosis">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           7\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Prognosis\n          </span>\n         </a>\n         <ul>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-24">\n           <a href="#Hip_fractures">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             7.1\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Hip fractures\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-25">\n           <a href="#Vertebral_fractures">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             7.2\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Vertebral fractures\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-26">\n           <a href="#Wrist_fractures">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             7.3\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Wrist fractures\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-27">\n           <a href="#Rib_fractures">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             7.4\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Rib fractures\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n         </ul>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-28">\n         <a href="#Epidemiology">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           8\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Epidemiology\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-29">\n         <a href="#History">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           9\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           History\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-30">\n         <a href="#References">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           10\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           References\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-31">\n         <a href="#External_links">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           11\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           External links\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n       </ul>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Signs_and_symptoms">\n        Signs and symptoms\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Osteoporosis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Signs and symptoms">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:722_Feature_Osteoprosis_of_Spine.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="492" data-file-width="610" height="177" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/722_Feature_Osteoprosis_of_Spine.jpg/220px-722_Feature_Osteoprosis_of_Spine.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/722_Feature_Osteoprosis_of_Spine.jpg/330px-722_Feature_Osteoprosis_of_Spine.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/722_Feature_Osteoprosis_of_Spine.jpg/440px-722_Feature_Osteoprosis_of_Spine.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:722_Feature_Osteoprosis_of_Spine.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Osteoporosis is an age-related disorder that causes the gradual loss of bone density and strength. When the thoracic vertebrae are affected, there can be a gradual collapse of the vertebrae. This results in kyphosis, an excessive curvature of the thoracic region.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Blausen_0686_Osteoporosis_01.png">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1024" data-file-width="768" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Blausen_0686_Osteoporosis_01.png/220px-Blausen_0686_Osteoporosis_01.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Blausen_0686_Osteoporosis_01.png/330px-Blausen_0686_Osteoporosis_01.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Blausen_0686_Osteoporosis_01.png/440px-Blausen_0686_Osteoporosis_01.png 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Blausen_0686_Osteoporosis_01.png" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Illustration depicting normal standing posture and osteoporosis\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Osteoporosis itself has\n       <a href="/wiki/Asymptomatic" title="Asymptomatic">\n        no symptoms\n       </a>\n       ; its main consequence is the increased risk of bone fractures. Osteoporotic\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fractures" title="Fractures">\n        fractures\n       </a>\n       occur in situations where healthy people would not normally break a bone; they are therefore regarded as fragility fractures. Typical fragility fractures occur in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Vertebral_column" title="Vertebral column">\n        vertebral column\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Rib" title="Rib">\n        rib\n       </a>\n       , hip and\n       <a href="/wiki/Wrist" title="Wrist">\n        wrist\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Fractures">\n        Fractures\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Osteoporosis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Fractures">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Fractures are the most dangerous aspect of osteoporosis. Debilitating acute and chronic pain in the elderly is often attributed to fractures from osteoporosis and can lead to further disability and early mortality.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">\n        <a href="#cite_note-16">\n         [16]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       These fractures may also be asymptomatic. The most common osteoporotic fractures are of the wrist, spine, shoulder and hip. The symptoms of a\n       <a href="/wiki/Vertebra" title="Vertebra">\n        vertebral\n       </a>\n       collapse ("\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Compression_fracture" title="Compression fracture">\n        compression fracture\n       </a>\n       ") are sudden\n       <a href="/wiki/Back_pain" title="Back pain">\n        back pain\n       </a>\n       , often with\n       <a href="/wiki/Radicular_pain" title="Radicular pain">\n        radicular pain\n       </a>\n       (shooting pain due to nerve root compression) and rarely with\n       <a href="/wiki/Spinal_cord_compression" title="Spinal cord compression">\n        spinal cord compression\n       </a>\n       or\n       <a href="/wiki/Cauda_equina_syndrome" title="Cauda equina syndrome">\n        cauda equina syndrome\n       </a>\n       . Multiple vertebral fractures lead to a stooped posture, loss of height, and chronic pain with resultant reduction in mobility.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">\n        <a href="#cite_note-17">\n         [17]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Fractures of the long bones acutely impair mobility and may require\n       <a href="/wiki/Surgery" title="Surgery">\n        surgery\n       </a>\n       .\n       <a href="/wiki/Hip_fracture" title="Hip fracture">\n        Hip fracture\n       </a>\n       , in particular, usually requires prompt surgery, as serious risks are associated with it, such as\n       <a href="/wiki/Deep_vein_thrombosis" title="Deep vein thrombosis">\n        deep vein thrombosis\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Pulmonary_embolism" title="Pulmonary embolism">\n        pulmonary embolism\n       </a>\n       , and increased mortality.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Fracture risk calculators assess the risk of fracture based upon several criteria, including\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bone_mineral_density" title="Bone mineral density">\n        BMD\n       </a>\n       , age, smoking, alcohol usage, weight, and gender. Recognized calculators include\n       <a href="/wiki/FRAX" title="FRAX">\n        FRAX\n       </a>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18">\n        <a href="#cite_note-18">\n         [18]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and Dubbo.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The term "established osteoporosis" is used when a\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fragility_fracture" title="Fragility fracture">\n        broken bone due to osteoporosis\n       </a>\n       has occurred.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHO1994_19-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-WHO1994-19">\n         [19]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Osteoporosis is a part of\n       <a href="/wiki/Frailty_syndrome" title="Frailty syndrome">\n        frailty syndrome\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Falls_risk">\n        Falls risk\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Osteoporosis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Falls risk">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       The increased risk of falling associated with aging leads to fractures of the wrist, spine, and hip. The risk of falling, in turn, is increased by impaired eyesight due to any cause (e.g.\n       <a href="/wiki/Glaucoma" title="Glaucoma">\n        glaucoma\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Macular_degeneration" title="Macular degeneration">\n        macular degeneration\n       </a>\n       ),\n       <a href="/wiki/Balance_disorder" title="Balance disorder">\n        balance disorder\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Movement_disorder" title="Movement disorder">\n        movement disorders\n       </a>\n       (e.g.\n       <a href="/wiki/Parkinson%27s_disease" title="Parkinson\'s disease">\n        Parkinson\'s disease\n       </a>\n       ),\n       <a href="/wiki/Dementia" title="Dementia">\n        dementia\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Sarcopenia" title="Sarcopenia">\n        sarcopenia\n       </a>\n       (age-related loss of\n       <a href="/wiki/Skeletal_muscle" title="Skeletal muscle">\n        skeletal muscle\n       </a>\n       ).\n       <a href="/wiki/Collapse_(medical)" title="Collapse (medical)">\n        Collapse\n       </a>\n       (transient loss of postural tone with or without loss of consciousness) leads to a significant risk of falls; causes of syncope are manifold, but may include\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cardiac_arrhythmia" title="Cardiac arrhythmia">\n        cardiac arrhythmias\n       </a>\n       (irregular heart beat),\n       <a href="/wiki/Vasovagal_syncope" title="Vasovagal syncope">\n        vasovagal syncope\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Orthostatic_hypotension" title="Orthostatic hypotension">\n        orthostatic hypotension\n       </a>\n       (abnormal drop in blood pressure on standing up), and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Seizure" title="Seizure">\n        seizures\n       </a>\n       . Removal of obstacles and loose carpets in the living environment may substantially reduce falls. Those with previous falls, as well as those with gait or balance disorders, are most at risk.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">\n        <a href="#cite_note-20">\n         [20]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Risk_factors">\n        Risk factors\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Osteoporosis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Risk factors">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       Risk factors for osteoporotic fracture can be split between nonmodifiable and (potentially) modifiable. In addition, osteoporosis is a recognized complication of specific diseases and disorders. Medication use is theoretically modifiable, although in many cases, the use of medication that increases osteoporosis risk may be unavoidable.\n       <a href="/wiki/Caffeine" title="Caffeine">\n        Caffeine\n       </a>\n       is not a risk factor for osteoporosis.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">\n        <a href="#cite_note-21">\n         [21]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       It is more likely in females than males.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NIH2014_3-22">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NIH2014-3">\n         [3]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Nonmodifiable">\n        Nonmodifiable\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Osteoporosis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Nonmodifiable">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:615_Age_and_Bone_Mass.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="553" data-file-width="860" height="141" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/615_Age_and_Bone_Mass.jpg/220px-615_Age_and_Bone_Mass.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/615_Age_and_Bone_Mass.jpg/330px-615_Age_and_Bone_Mass.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/615_Age_and_Bone_Mass.jpg/440px-615_Age_and_Bone_Mass.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:615_Age_and_Bone_Mass.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Bone density peaks at about 30 years of age. Women lose bone mass more rapidly than men.\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">\n          <a href="#cite_note-22">\n           [22]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        The most important risk factors for osteoporosis are advanced age (in both men and women) and\n        <a href="/wiki/Female" title="Female">\n         female\n        </a>\n        sex;\n        <a href="/wiki/Estrogen" title="Estrogen">\n         estrogen\n        </a>\n        deficiency following menopause or\n        <a href="/wiki/Oophorectomy" title="Oophorectomy">\n         surgical removal of the ovaries\n        </a>\n        is correlated with a rapid reduction in bone mineral density, while in men, a decrease in\n        <a href="/wiki/Testosterone" title="Testosterone">\n         testosterone\n        </a>\n        levels has a comparable (but less pronounced) effect.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">\n         <a href="#cite_note-23">\n          [23]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">\n         <a href="#cite_note-24">\n          [24]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Race: While osteoporosis occurs in people from all ethnic groups,\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/European_ethnic_groups" title="European ethnic groups">\n         European\n        </a>\n        or\n        <a href="/wiki/Asian_people" title="Asian people">\n         Asian\n        </a>\n        ancestry predisposes for osteoporosis.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">\n         <a href="#cite_note-25">\n          [25]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Heredity: Those with a\n        <a href="/wiki/Family_history_(medicine)" title="Family history (medicine)">\n         family history\n        </a>\n        of fracture or osteoporosis are at an increased risk; the\n        <a href="/wiki/Heritability" title="Heritability">\n         heritability\n        </a>\n        of the fracture, as well as low bone mineral density, is relatively high, ranging from 25 to 80%. At least 30 genes are associated with the development of osteoporosis.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Raisz_26-0">\n         <a href="#cite_note-Raisz-26">\n          [26]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Those who have already had a fracture are at least twice as likely to have another fracture compared to someone of the same age and sex.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27">\n         <a href="#cite_note-27">\n          [27]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        Early menopause/hysterectomy is another predisposing factor.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Build: A small stature is also a nonmodifiable risk factor associated with the development of osteoporosis.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AppTher_28-0">\n         <a href="#cite_note-AppTher-28">\n          [28]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Potentially_modifiable">\n        Potentially modifiable\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Osteoporosis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Potentially modifiable">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        Excess consumption of alcohol: Although small amounts of alcohol are probably beneficial (bone density increases with increasing alcohol intake), chronic heavy drinking (alcohol intake greater than three units/day) probably increases fracture risk despite any beneficial effects on bone density.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BMJosteoporosis_29-0">\n         <a href="#cite_note-BMJosteoporosis-29">\n          [29]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30">\n         <a href="#cite_note-30">\n          [30]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Vitamin_D_deficiency" title="Vitamin D deficiency">\n         Vitamin D deficiency\n        </a>\n        :\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-micronutrients_31-0">\n         <a href="#cite_note-micronutrients-31">\n          [31]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32">\n         <a href="#cite_note-32">\n          [32]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        Low circulating Vitamin D is common among the elderly worldwide.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHOcriteria_4-3">\n         <a href="#cite_note-WHOcriteria-4">\n          [4]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        Mild vitamin D insufficiency is associated with increased\n        <a href="/wiki/Parathyroid_hormone" title="Parathyroid hormone">\n         parathyroid hormone\n        </a>\n        (PTH) production.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHOcriteria_4-4">\n         <a href="#cite_note-WHOcriteria-4">\n          [4]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        PTH increases bone resorption, leading to bone loss. A positive association exists between serum\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1,25-dihydroxycholecalciferol" title="1,25-dihydroxycholecalciferol">\n         1,25-dihydroxycholecalciferol\n        </a>\n        levels and bone mineral density, while PTH is negatively associated with bone mineral density.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHOcriteria_4-5">\n         <a href="#cite_note-WHOcriteria-4">\n          [4]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Tobacco_smoking" title="Tobacco smoking">\n         Tobacco smoking\n        </a>\n        : Many studies have associated smoking with decreased bone health, but the mechanisms are unclear. Tobacco smoking has been proposed to inhibit the activity of osteoblasts, and is an independent risk factor for osteoporosis.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BMJosteoporosis_29-1">\n         <a href="#cite_note-BMJosteoporosis-29">\n          [29]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33">\n         <a href="#cite_note-33">\n          [33]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        Smoking also results in increased breakdown of exogenous estrogen, lower body weight and earlier menopause, all of which contribute to lower bone mineral density.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHOcriteria_4-6">\n         <a href="#cite_note-WHOcriteria-4">\n          [4]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Malnutrition" title="Malnutrition">\n         Malnutrition\n        </a>\n        : Nutrition has an important and complex role in maintenance of good bone. Identified risk factors include low dietary\n        <a href="/wiki/Calcium" title="Calcium">\n         calcium\n        </a>\n        and/or phosphorus, magnesium, zinc, boron, iron, fluoride, copper, vitamins A, K, E and C (and D where skin exposure to sunlight provides an inadequate supply). Excess sodium is a risk factor. High blood acidity may be diet-related, and is a known antagonist of bone.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pmid11194525_34-0">\n         <a href="#cite_note-pmid11194525-34">\n          [34]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        Some have identified low protein intake as associated with lower peak bone mass during adolescence and lower bone mineral density in elderly populations.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHOcriteria_4-7">\n         <a href="#cite_note-WHOcriteria-4">\n          [4]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        Conversely, some have identified low protein intake as a positive factor, protein is among the causes of dietary acidity. Imbalance of omega-6 to omega-3 polyunsaturated fats is yet another identified risk factor.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35">\n         <a href="#cite_note-35">\n          [35]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        High\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Protein_in_nutrition" title="Protein in nutrition">\n         dietary protein\n        </a>\n        from animal sources: Research has found an association between diets high in animal protein and increased urinary calcium,\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36">\n         <a href="#cite_note-36">\n          [36]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37">\n         <a href="#cite_note-37">\n          [37]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">\n         <a href="#cite_note-38">\n          [38]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        and have been linked to an increase in fractures.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39">\n         <a href="#cite_note-39">\n          [39]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        However, the relevance of this observation to bone density is unclear\n        <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n         [\n         <i>\n          <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n           <span title="the next citation relates only to protein in general, not animal protein specifically (April 2015)">\n            citation needed\n           </span>\n          </a>\n         </i>\n         ]\n        </sup>\n        , since higher protein diets tend to increase absorption of calcium from the diet and are associated with higher bone density.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40">\n         <a href="#cite_note-40">\n          [40]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        Indeed, it has recently been argued that low protein diets cause poor bone health.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41">\n         <a href="#cite_note-41">\n          [41]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        No interventional trials have been performed on dietary protein in the prevention and treatment of osteoporosis.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pmid12936953_42-0">\n         <a href="#cite_note-pmid12936953-42">\n          [42]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Body_mass_index" title="Body mass index">\n         Underweight\n        </a>\n        /\n        <a href="/wiki/Physical_exercise" title="Physical exercise">\n         inactive\n        </a>\n        :\n        <a href="/wiki/Bone_remodeling" title="Bone remodeling">\n         Bone remodeling\n        </a>\n        occurs in response to physical stress, so physical inactivity can lead to significant bone loss.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHOcriteria_4-8">\n         <a href="#cite_note-WHOcriteria-4">\n          [4]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Weight_bearing" title="Weight bearing">\n         Weight bearing\n        </a>\n        exercise can increase peak bone mass achieved in adolescence,\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHOcriteria_4-9">\n         <a href="#cite_note-WHOcriteria-4">\n          [4]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        and a highly significant correlation between bone strength and muscle strength has been determined.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43">\n         <a href="#cite_note-43">\n          [43]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        The incidence of osteoporosis is lower in overweight people.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44">\n         <a href="#cite_note-44">\n          [44]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Endurance training: In female endurance athletes, large volumes of training can lead to decreased bone density and an increased risk of osteoporosis.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45">\n         <a href="#cite_note-45">\n          [45]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        This effect might be caused by intense training suppressing menstruation, producing\n        <a href="/wiki/Amenorrhea" title="Amenorrhea">\n         amenorrhea\n        </a>\n        , and it is part of the\n        <a href="/wiki/Female_athlete_triad" title="Female athlete triad">\n         female athlete triad\n        </a>\n        .\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46">\n         <a href="#cite_note-46">\n          [46]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        However, for male athletes, the situation is less clear, and although some studies have reported low bone density in elite male endurance athletes,\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47">\n         <a href="#cite_note-47">\n          [47]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        others have instead seen increased leg bone density.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48">\n         <a href="#cite_note-48">\n          [48]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49">\n         <a href="#cite_note-49">\n          [49]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Heavy_metals" title="Heavy metals">\n         Heavy metals\n        </a>\n        : A strong association between\n        <a href="/wiki/Cadmium" title="Cadmium">\n         cadmium\n        </a>\n        and\n        <a href="/wiki/Lead" title="Lead">\n         lead\n        </a>\n        with bone disease has been established. Low-level exposure to cadmium is associated with an increased loss of bone mineral density readily in both genders, leading to pain and increased risk of fractures, especially in the elderly and in females. Higher cadmium exposure results in\n        <a href="/wiki/Osteomalacia" title="Osteomalacia">\n         osteomalacia\n        </a>\n        (softening of the bone).\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50">\n         <a href="#cite_note-50">\n          [50]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Soft drinks: Some studies indicate\n        <a href="/wiki/Soft_drink" title="Soft drink">\n         soft drinks\n        </a>\n        (many of which contain\n        <a href="/wiki/Phosphoric_acid" title="Phosphoric acid">\n         phosphoric acid\n        </a>\n        ) may increase risk of osteoporosis, at least in\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Women" title="Women">\n         women\n        </a>\n        .\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51">\n         <a href="#cite_note-51">\n          [51]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        Others suggest soft drinks may displace calcium-containing drinks from the diet rather than directly causing osteoporosis.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52">\n         <a href="#cite_note-52">\n          [52]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Proton_pump_inhibitors" title="Proton pump inhibitors">\n         Proton pump inhibitors\n        </a>\n        (such as\n        <a href="/wiki/Lansoprazole" title="Lansoprazole">\n         lansoprazole\n        </a>\n        ,\n        <a href="/wiki/Esomeprazole" title="Esomeprazole">\n         esomeprazole\n        </a>\n        , or\n        <a href="/wiki/Omeprazole" title="Omeprazole">\n         omeprazole\n        </a>\n        ) that decrease\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stomach_acid" title="Stomach acid">\n         stomach acid\n        </a>\n        , are a risk for bone fractures if taken for two or more years, due to decreased absorption of\n        <a href="/wiki/Calcium" title="Calcium">\n         calcium\n        </a>\n        in the\n        <a href="/wiki/Stomach" title="Stomach">\n         stomach\n        </a>\n        .\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53">\n         <a href="#cite_note-53">\n          [53]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Medical_disorders">\n        Medical disorders\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Osteoporosis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Medical disorders">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:312px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:625_Calcium_Homeostasis.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="737" data-file-width="825" height="277" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/625_Calcium_Homeostasis.jpg/310px-625_Calcium_Homeostasis.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/625_Calcium_Homeostasis.jpg/465px-625_Calcium_Homeostasis.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/625_Calcium_Homeostasis.jpg/620px-625_Calcium_Homeostasis.jpg 2x" width="310"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:625_Calcium_Homeostasis.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         The body regulates calcium homeostasis with two pathways; one is signaled to turn on when blood calcium levels drop below normal and one is the pathway that is signaled to turn on when blood calcium levels are elevated.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Many diseases and disorders have been associated with osteoporosis.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ICSI_54-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ICSI-54">\n         [54]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       For some, the underlying mechanism influencing the bone metabolism is straightforward, whereas for others the causes are multiple or unknown.\n      </p>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        In general,\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Muscle_immobilization" title="Muscle immobilization">\n         immobilization\n        </a>\n        causes bone loss (following the \'use it or lose it\' rule). For example, localized osteoporosis can occur after prolonged immobilization of a fractured limb in a cast. This is also more common in active people with a high bone turn-over (for example, athletes). Other examples include bone loss during\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Space_flight" title="Space flight">\n         space flight\n        </a>\n        or in people who are bedridden or use wheelchairs for various reasons.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Hypogonadism" title="Hypogonadism">\n         Hypogonadal\n        </a>\n        states can cause secondary osteoporosis. These include\n        <a href="/wiki/Turner_syndrome" title="Turner syndrome">\n         Turner syndrome\n        </a>\n        ,\n        <a href="/wiki/Klinefelter_syndrome" title="Klinefelter syndrome">\n         Klinefelter syndrome\n        </a>\n        ,\n        <a href="/wiki/Kallmann_syndrome" title="Kallmann syndrome">\n         Kallmann syndrome\n        </a>\n        ,\n        <a href="/wiki/Anorexia_nervosa" title="Anorexia nervosa">\n         anorexia nervosa\n        </a>\n        ,\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Andropause" title="Andropause">\n         andropause\n        </a>\n        ,\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-medscapeosteoporosis_55-0">\n         <a href="#cite_note-medscapeosteoporosis-55">\n          [55]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        <a href="/wiki/Hypothalamus" title="Hypothalamus">\n         hypothalamic\n        </a>\n        amenorrhea or\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hyperprolactinemia" title="Hyperprolactinemia">\n         hyperprolactinemia\n        </a>\n        .\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-medscapeosteoporosis_55-1">\n         <a href="#cite_note-medscapeosteoporosis-55">\n          [55]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        In females, the effect of hypogonadism is mediated by estrogen deficiency. It can appear as early menopause (&lt;45 years) or from prolonged premenopausal amenorrhea (&gt;1 year). Bilateral\n        <a href="/wiki/Oophorectomy" title="Oophorectomy">\n         oophorectomy\n        </a>\n        (surgical removal of the ovaries) and\n        <a href="/wiki/Premature_ovarian_failure" title="Premature ovarian failure">\n         premature ovarian failure\n        </a>\n        cause deficient estrogen production. In males, testosterone deficiency is the cause (for example, andropause or after surgical removal of the\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Testes" title="Testes">\n         testes\n        </a>\n        ).\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Endocrine disorders that can induce bone loss include\n        <a href="/wiki/Cushing%27s_syndrome" title="Cushing\'s syndrome">\n         Cushing\'s syndrome\n        </a>\n        ,\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHOcriteria_4-10">\n         <a href="#cite_note-WHOcriteria-4">\n          [4]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        <a href="/wiki/Hyperparathyroidism" title="Hyperparathyroidism">\n         hyperparathyroidism\n        </a>\n        ,\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHOcriteria_4-11">\n         <a href="#cite_note-WHOcriteria-4">\n          [4]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        <a href="/wiki/Hyperthyroidism" title="Hyperthyroidism">\n         hyperthyroidism\n        </a>\n        ,\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHOcriteria_4-12">\n         <a href="#cite_note-WHOcriteria-4">\n          [4]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        <a href="/wiki/Hypothyroidism" title="Hypothyroidism">\n         hypothyroidism\n        </a>\n        ,\n        <a href="/wiki/Diabetes_mellitus" title="Diabetes mellitus">\n         diabetes mellitus\n        </a>\n        type 1 and 2,\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OsteoporosisMen_56-0">\n         <a href="#cite_note-OsteoporosisMen-56">\n          [56]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        <a href="/wiki/Acromegaly" title="Acromegaly">\n         acromegaly\n        </a>\n        , and\n        <a href="/wiki/Adrenal_insufficiency" title="Adrenal insufficiency">\n         adrenal insufficiency\n        </a>\n        .\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ICSI_54-1">\n         <a href="#cite_note-ICSI-54">\n          [54]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Malnutrition,\n        <a href="/wiki/Parenteral_nutrition" title="Parenteral nutrition">\n         parenteral nutrition\n        </a>\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHOcriteria_4-13">\n         <a href="#cite_note-WHOcriteria-4">\n          [4]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        and\n        <a href="/wiki/Malabsorption" title="Malabsorption">\n         malabsorption\n        </a>\n        can lead to osteoporosis. Nutritional and gastrointestinal disorders that can predispose to osteoporosis include undiagnosed and untreated\n        <a href="/wiki/Coeliac_disease" title="Coeliac disease">\n         coeliac disease\n        </a>\n        (both symptomatic and asymptomatic people),\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHOcriteria_4-14">\n         <a href="#cite_note-WHOcriteria-4">\n          [4]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MirzaCanalis2015_57-0">\n         <a href="#cite_note-MirzaCanalis2015-57">\n          [57]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        <a href="/wiki/Crohn%27s_disease" title="Crohn\'s disease">\n         Crohn\'s disease\n        </a>\n        ,\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pediatric_58-0">\n         <a href="#cite_note-Pediatric-58">\n          [58]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        <a href="/wiki/Ulcerative_colitis" title="Ulcerative colitis">\n         ulcerative colitis\n        </a>\n        ,\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pediatric_58-1">\n         <a href="#cite_note-Pediatric-58">\n          [58]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        <a href="/wiki/Cystic_fibrosis" title="Cystic fibrosis">\n         cystic fibrosis\n        </a>\n        ,\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pediatric_58-2">\n         <a href="#cite_note-Pediatric-58">\n          [58]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        surgery\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-medscapeosteoporosis_55-2">\n         <a href="#cite_note-medscapeosteoporosis-55">\n          [55]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        (after\n        <a href="/wiki/Gastrectomy" title="Gastrectomy">\n         gastrectomy\n        </a>\n        ,\n        <a href="/wiki/Partial_ileal_bypass_surgery" title="Partial ileal bypass surgery">\n         intestinal bypass surgery\n        </a>\n        or\n        <a href="/wiki/Bowel_resection" title="Bowel resection">\n         bowel resection\n        </a>\n        ) and severe\n        <a href="/wiki/Liver_disease" title="Liver disease">\n         liver disease\n        </a>\n        (especially\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Primary_biliary_cirrhosis" title="Primary biliary cirrhosis">\n         primary biliary cirrhosis\n        </a>\n        ).\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-medscapeosteoporosis_55-3">\n         <a href="#cite_note-medscapeosteoporosis-55">\n          [55]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        People with\n        <a href="/wiki/Lactose_intolerance" title="Lactose intolerance">\n         lactose intolerance\n        </a>\n        or\n        <a href="/wiki/Milk_allergy" title="Milk allergy">\n         milk allergy\n        </a>\n        may develop osteoporosis due to restrictions of calcium-containing foods.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Beto2015_59-0">\n         <a href="#cite_note-Beto2015-59">\n          [59]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        Individuals with\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bulimia" title="Bulimia">\n         bulimia\n        </a>\n        can also develop osteoporosis. Those with an otherwise adequate calcium intake can develop osteoporosis due to the inability to absorb calcium and/or vitamin D. Other micronutrients such as\n        <a href="/wiki/Vitamin_K" title="Vitamin K">\n         vitamin K\n        </a>\n        or\n        <a href="/wiki/Vitamin_B12_deficiency" title="Vitamin B12 deficiency">\n         vitamin B\n         <sub>\n          12\n         </sub>\n         deficiency\n        </a>\n        may also contribute.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        People with rheumatologic disorders such as\n        <a href="/wiki/Rheumatoid_arthritis" title="Rheumatoid arthritis">\n         rheumatoid arthritis\n        </a>\n        ,\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-medscapeosteoporosis_55-4">\n         <a href="#cite_note-medscapeosteoporosis-55">\n          [55]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        <a href="/wiki/Ankylosing_spondylitis" title="Ankylosing spondylitis">\n         ankylosing spondylitis\n        </a>\n        ,\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-medscapeosteoporosis_55-5">\n         <a href="#cite_note-medscapeosteoporosis-55">\n          [55]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        <a href="/wiki/Systemic_lupus_erythematosus" title="Systemic lupus erythematosus">\n         systemic lupus erythematosus\n        </a>\n        and polyarticular\n        <a href="/wiki/Juvenile_idiopathic_arthritis" title="Juvenile idiopathic arthritis">\n         juvenile idiopathic arthritis\n        </a>\n        are at increased risk of osteoporosis, either as part of their disease or because of other risk factors (notably corticosteroid therapy). Systemic diseases such as\n        <a href="/wiki/Amyloidosis" title="Amyloidosis">\n         amyloidosis\n        </a>\n        and\n        <a href="/wiki/Sarcoidosis" title="Sarcoidosis">\n         sarcoidosis\n        </a>\n        can also lead to osteoporosis.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Renal_insufficiency" title="Renal insufficiency">\n         Renal insufficiency\n        </a>\n        can lead to\n        <a href="/wiki/Renal_osteodystrophy" title="Renal osteodystrophy">\n         renal osteodystrophy\n        </a>\n        .\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Hematologic disorders linked to osteoporosis are\n        <a href="/wiki/Multiple_myeloma" title="Multiple myeloma">\n         multiple myeloma\n        </a>\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-medscapeosteoporosis_55-6">\n         <a href="#cite_note-medscapeosteoporosis-55">\n          [55]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        and other\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Monoclonal_gammopathy" title="Monoclonal gammopathy">\n         monoclonal gammopathies\n        </a>\n        ,\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OsteoporosisMen_56-1">\n         <a href="#cite_note-OsteoporosisMen-56">\n          [56]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        <a href="/wiki/Lymphoma" title="Lymphoma">\n         lymphoma\n        </a>\n        ,\n        <a href="/wiki/Leukemia" title="Leukemia">\n         leukemia\n        </a>\n        ,\n        <a href="/wiki/Mastocytosis" title="Mastocytosis">\n         mastocytosis\n        </a>\n        ,\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-medscapeosteoporosis_55-7">\n         <a href="#cite_note-medscapeosteoporosis-55">\n          [55]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hemophilia" title="Hemophilia">\n         hemophilia\n        </a>\n        ,\n        <a href="/wiki/Sickle-cell_disease" title="Sickle-cell disease">\n         sickle-cell disease\n        </a>\n        and\n        <a href="/wiki/Thalassemia" title="Thalassemia">\n         thalassemia\n        </a>\n        .\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Several inherited disorders have been linked to osteoporosis. These include\n        <a href="/wiki/Osteogenesis_imperfecta" title="Osteogenesis imperfecta">\n         osteogenesis imperfecta\n        </a>\n        ,\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-medscapeosteoporosis_55-8">\n         <a href="#cite_note-medscapeosteoporosis-55">\n          [55]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        <a href="/wiki/Marfan_syndrome" title="Marfan syndrome">\n         Marfan syndrome\n        </a>\n        ,\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-medscapeosteoporosis_55-9">\n         <a href="#cite_note-medscapeosteoporosis-55">\n          [55]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hemochromatosis" title="Hemochromatosis">\n         hemochromatosis\n        </a>\n        ,\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHOcriteria_4-15">\n         <a href="#cite_note-WHOcriteria-4">\n          [4]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        <a href="/wiki/Hypophosphatasia" title="Hypophosphatasia">\n         hypophosphatasia\n        </a>\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60">\n         <a href="#cite_note-60">\n          [60]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        (for which it is often misdiagnosed),\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61">\n         <a href="#cite_note-61">\n          [61]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        <a href="/wiki/Glycogen_storage_disease" title="Glycogen storage disease">\n         glycogen storage diseases\n        </a>\n        ,\n        <a href="/wiki/Homocystinuria" title="Homocystinuria">\n         homocystinuria\n        </a>\n        ,\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-medscapeosteoporosis_55-10">\n         <a href="#cite_note-medscapeosteoporosis-55">\n          [55]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ehlers%E2%80%93Danlos_syndrome" title="Ehlers\xe2\x80\x93Danlos syndrome">\n         Ehlers\xe2\x80\x93Danlos syndrome\n        </a>\n        ,\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-medscapeosteoporosis_55-11">\n         <a href="#cite_note-medscapeosteoporosis-55">\n          [55]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        <a href="/wiki/Porphyria" title="Porphyria">\n         porphyria\n        </a>\n        ,\n        <a href="/wiki/Menkes_disease" title="Menkes disease">\n         Menkes\' syndrome\n        </a>\n        ,\n        <a href="/wiki/Epidermolysis_bullosa" title="Epidermolysis bullosa">\n         epidermolysis bullosa\n        </a>\n        and\n        <a href="/wiki/Gaucher%27s_disease" title="Gaucher\'s disease">\n         Gaucher\'s disease\n        </a>\n        .\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        People with\n        <a href="/wiki/Scoliosis" title="Scoliosis">\n         scoliosis\n        </a>\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Idiopathic" title="Idiopathic">\n         of unknown cause\n        </a>\n        also have a higher risk of osteoporosis. Bone loss can be a feature of\n        <a href="/wiki/Complex_regional_pain_syndrome" title="Complex regional pain syndrome">\n         complex regional pain syndrome\n        </a>\n        . It is also more frequent in people with Parkinson\'s disease and\n        <a href="/wiki/Chronic_obstructive_pulmonary_disease" title="Chronic obstructive pulmonary disease">\n         chronic obstructive pulmonary disease\n        </a>\n        .\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        People with\n        <a href="/wiki/Parkinson%27s_disease" title="Parkinson\'s disease">\n         Parkinson\'s disease\n        </a>\n        have a higher risk of broken bones. This is related to poor balance and poor bone density.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62">\n         <a href="#cite_note-62">\n          [62]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        In Parkinson\xe2\x80\x99s disease there may be a link between the loss of\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dopaminergic_neuron" title="Dopaminergic neuron">\n         dopaminergic neurons\n        </a>\n        and altered\n        <a href="/wiki/Calcium_metabolism" title="Calcium metabolism">\n         calcium metabolism\n        </a>\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63">\n         <a href="#cite_note-63">\n          [63]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        (and\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Iron_metabolism" title="Iron metabolism">\n         iron metabolism\n        </a>\n        ) causing a stiffening of the skeleton and\n        <a href="/wiki/Kyphosis" title="Kyphosis">\n         kyphosis\n        </a>\n        .\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Medication">\n        Medication\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Osteoporosis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Medication">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Certain medications have been associated with an increase in osteoporosis risk; only glucocorticosteroids and anticonvulsants are classically associated, but evidence is emerging with regard to other drugs.\n      </p>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Steroid-induced_osteoporosis" title="Steroid-induced osteoporosis">\n         Steroid-induced osteoporosis\n        </a>\n        (SIOP) arises due to use of glucocorticoids\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x93 analogous to Cushing\'s syndrome and involving mainly the axial skeleton. The synthetic glucocorticoid prescription drug\n        <a href="/wiki/Prednisone" title="Prednisone">\n         prednisone\n        </a>\n        is a main candidate after prolonged intake. Some professional guidelines recommend prophylaxis in patients who take the equivalent of more than 30\xc2\xa0mg hydrocortisone (7.5\xc2\xa0mg of prednisolone), especially when this is in excess of three months.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64">\n         <a href="#cite_note-64">\n          [64]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        Alternate day use may not prevent this complication.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GIOP_65-0">\n         <a href="#cite_note-GIOP-65">\n          [65]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Barbiturate" title="Barbiturate">\n         Barbiturates\n        </a>\n        ,\n        <a href="/wiki/Phenytoin" title="Phenytoin">\n         phenytoin\n        </a>\n        and some other enzyme-inducing\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Antiepileptic" title="Antiepileptic">\n         antiepileptics\n        </a>\n        \xe2\x80\x93 these probably accelerate the metabolism of vitamin D.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66">\n         <a href="#cite_note-66">\n          [66]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/L-Thyroxine" title="L-Thyroxine">\n         L-Thyroxine\n        </a>\n        over-replacement may contribute to osteoporosis, in a similar fashion as thyrotoxicosis does.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ICSI_54-2">\n         <a href="#cite_note-ICSI-54">\n          [54]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        This can be relevant in subclinical hypothyroidism.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Several drugs induce hypogonadism, for example\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aromatase_inhibitors" title="Aromatase inhibitors">\n         aromatase inhibitors\n        </a>\n        used in breast cancer,\n        <a href="/wiki/Methotrexate" title="Methotrexate">\n         methotrexate\n        </a>\n        and other antimetabolite drugs,\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Depo-Provera" title="Depo-Provera">\n         depot progesterone\n        </a>\n        and\n        <a href="/wiki/Gonadotropin-releasing_hormone_agonist" title="Gonadotropin-releasing hormone agonist">\n         gonadotropin-releasing hormone agonists\n        </a>\n        .\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Anticoagulant" title="Anticoagulant">\n         Anticoagulants\n        </a>\n        \xe2\x80\x93 long-term use of heparin is associated with a decrease in bone density,\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67">\n         <a href="#cite_note-67">\n          [67]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        and\n        <a href="/wiki/Warfarin" title="Warfarin">\n         warfarin\n        </a>\n        (and related coumarins) have been linked with an increased risk in osteoporotic fracture in long-term use.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68">\n         <a href="#cite_note-68">\n          [68]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Proton_pump_inhibitors" title="Proton pump inhibitors">\n         Proton pump inhibitors\n        </a>\n        \xe2\x80\x93 these drugs inhibit the production of\n        <a href="/wiki/Gastric_acid" title="Gastric acid">\n         stomach acid\n        </a>\n        ; this is thought to interfere with calcium absorption.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69">\n         <a href="#cite_note-69">\n          [69]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        Chronic\n        <a href="/wiki/Phosphate" title="Phosphate">\n         phosphate\n        </a>\n        binding may also occur with\n        <a href="/wiki/Aluminium" title="Aluminium">\n         aluminium\n        </a>\n        -containing\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Antacids" title="Antacids">\n         antacids\n        </a>\n        .\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ICSI_54-3">\n         <a href="#cite_note-ICSI-54">\n          [54]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Thiazolidinedione" title="Thiazolidinedione">\n         Thiazolidinediones\n        </a>\n        (used for diabetes) \xe2\x80\x93\n        <a href="/wiki/Rosiglitazone" title="Rosiglitazone">\n         rosiglitazone\n        </a>\n        and possibly\n        <a href="/wiki/Pioglitazone" title="Pioglitazone">\n         pioglitazone\n        </a>\n        , inhibitors of\n        <a href="/wiki/Peroxisome_proliferator-activated_receptor_gamma" title="Peroxisome proliferator-activated receptor gamma">\n         PPAR\xce\xb3\n        </a>\n        , have been linked with an increased risk of osteoporosis and fracture.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70">\n         <a href="#cite_note-70">\n          [70]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Chronic\n        <a href="/wiki/Lithium" title="Lithium">\n         lithium\n        </a>\n        therapy has been associated with osteoporosis.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ICSI_54-4">\n         <a href="#cite_note-ICSI-54">\n          [54]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Evolutionary">\n        Evolutionary\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Osteoporosis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Evolutionary">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Age-related bone loss is common among humans due to exhibiting less dense bones than other primate species.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Latimer_2005_71-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Latimer_2005-71">\n         [71]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Because of the more porous bones of humans, frequency of severe osteoporosis and osteoporosis related fractures is higher.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cot2011_72-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Cot2011-72">\n         [72]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The human vulnerability to osteoporosis is an obvious cost but it can be justified by the advantage of bipedalism inferring that this vulnerability is the byproduct of such.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cot2011_72-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Cot2011-72">\n         [72]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       It has been suggested that porous bones help to absorb the increased stress that we have on two surfaces compared to our primate counterparts who have four surfaces to disperse the force.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Latimer_2005_71-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Latimer_2005-71">\n         [71]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In addition, the porosity allows for more flexibility and a lighter skeleton that is easier to support.\n
