      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cot2011_72-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Cot2011-72">\n         [72]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       One other consideration may be that diets today have much lower amounts of calcium than the diets of other primates or the tetrapedal ancestors to humans which may lead to higher likelihood to show signs of osteoporosis.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pmid2053574_73-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-pmid2053574-73">\n         [73]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Pathogenesis">\n        Pathogenesis\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Osteoporosis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Pathogenesis">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Osteoporosis_Locations.png">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1200" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Osteoporosis_Locations.png/220px-Osteoporosis_Locations.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Osteoporosis_Locations.png/330px-Osteoporosis_Locations.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Osteoporosis_Locations.png/440px-Osteoporosis_Locations.png 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Osteoporosis_Locations.png" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Osteoporosis locations\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Osteoclast.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="257" data-file-width="481" height="118" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Osteoclast.jpg/220px-Osteoclast.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Osteoclast.jpg/330px-Osteoclast.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Osteoclast.jpg/440px-Osteoclast.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Osteoclast.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <a href="/wiki/Micrograph" title="Micrograph">\n          Light micrograph\n         </a>\n         of an osteoclast displaying typical distinguishing characteristics: a large cell with multiple nuclei and a "foamy" cytosol.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Active_osteoblasts.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="520" data-file-width="800" height="143" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Active_osteoblasts.jpg/220px-Active_osteoblasts.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Active_osteoblasts.jpg/330px-Active_osteoblasts.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Active_osteoblasts.jpg/440px-Active_osteoblasts.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Active_osteoblasts.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <a href="/wiki/Micrograph" title="Micrograph">\n          Light micrograph\n         </a>\n         of\n         <a href="/wiki/Osteoblast" title="Osteoblast">\n          osteoblasts\n         </a>\n         , several displaying a prominent\n         <a href="/wiki/Golgi_apparatus" title="Golgi apparatus">\n          Golgi apparatus\n         </a>\n         , actively synthesizing\n         <a href="/wiki/Osteoid" title="Osteoid">\n          osteoid\n         </a>\n         containing two\n         <a href="/wiki/Osteocyte" title="Osteocyte">\n          osteocytes\n         </a>\n         .\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The underlying mechanism in all cases of osteoporosis is an imbalance between\n       <a href="/wiki/Bone_resorption" title="Bone resorption">\n        bone resorption\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bone_development" title="Bone development">\n        bone formation\n       </a>\n       . In normal bone,\n       <a href="/wiki/Matrix_(biology)" title="Matrix (biology)">\n        matrix\n       </a>\n       remodeling of bone is constant; up to 10% of all bone mass may be undergoing remodeling at any point in time. The process takes place in bone multicellular units (BMUs) as first described by Frost &amp; Thomas in 1963.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74">\n        <a href="#cite_note-74">\n         [74]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Osteoclasts" title="Osteoclasts">\n        Osteoclasts\n       </a>\n       are assisted by transcription factor PU.1 to degrade the bone matrix, while\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Osteoblasts" title="Osteoblasts">\n        osteoblasts\n       </a>\n       rebuild the bone matrix. Low bone mass density can then occur when osteoclasts are degrading the bone matrix faster than the osteoblasts are rebuilding the bone.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75">\n        <a href="#cite_note-75">\n         [75]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The three main mechanisms by which osteoporosis develops are an inadequate peak bone mass (the skeleton develops insufficient mass and strength during growth), excessive bone resorption, and inadequate formation of new bone during remodeling, likely due to MSC biasing away from the\n       <a href="/wiki/Osteoblast" title="Osteoblast">\n        osteoblast\n       </a>\n       and toward the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marrow_Adipose_Tissue" title="Marrow Adipose Tissue">\n        marrow adipocyte\n       </a>\n       lineage.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76">\n        <a href="#cite_note-76">\n         [76]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       An interplay of these three mechanisms underlies the development of fragile bone tissue.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Raisz_26-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Raisz-26">\n         [26]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Hormonal factors strongly determine the rate of bone resorption; lack of estrogen (e.g. as a result of menopause) increases bone resorption, as well as decreasing the deposition of new bone that normally takes place in weight-bearing bones. The amount of estrogen needed to suppress this process is lower than that normally needed to stimulate the\n       <a href="/wiki/Uterus" title="Uterus">\n        uterus\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Mammary_gland" title="Mammary gland">\n        breast gland\n       </a>\n       . The \xce\xb1-form of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Estrogen_receptor" title="Estrogen receptor">\n        estrogen receptor\n       </a>\n       appears to be the most important in regulating bone turnover.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Raisz_26-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Raisz-26">\n         [26]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In addition to estrogen,\n       <a href="/wiki/Calcium_metabolism" title="Calcium metabolism">\n        calcium metabolism\n       </a>\n       plays a significant role in bone turnover, and deficiency of calcium and vitamin D leads to impaired bone deposition; in addition, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Parathyroid_gland" title="Parathyroid gland">\n        parathyroid glands\n       </a>\n       react to low calcium levels by secreting parathyroid hormone (parathormone, PTH), which increases bone resorption to ensure sufficient calcium in the blood. The role of\n       <a href="/wiki/Calcitonin" title="Calcitonin">\n        calcitonin\n       </a>\n       , a hormone generated by the\n       <a href="/wiki/Thyroid" title="Thyroid">\n        thyroid\n       </a>\n       that increases bone deposition, is less clear and probably not as significant as that of PTH.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Raisz_26-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Raisz-26">\n         [26]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The activation of osteoclasts is regulated by various molecular signals, of which\n       <a href="/wiki/RANKL" title="RANKL">\n        RANKL\n       </a>\n       (receptor activator of\n       <a href="/wiki/NF-%CE%BAB" title="NF-\xce\xbaB">\n        nuclear factor kappa-B\n       </a>\n       ligand) is one of the best studied. This molecule is produced by osteoblasts and other cells (e.g.\n       <a href="/wiki/Lymphocyte" title="Lymphocyte">\n        lymphocytes\n       </a>\n       ), and stimulates\n       <a href="/wiki/RANK" title="RANK">\n        RANK\n       </a>\n       (receptor activator of nuclear factor \xce\xbaB).\n       <a href="/wiki/Osteoprotegerin" title="Osteoprotegerin">\n        Osteoprotegerin\n       </a>\n       (OPG) binds RANKL before it has an opportunity to bind to RANK, and hence suppresses its ability to increase bone resorption. RANKL, RANK and OPG are closely related to\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tumor_necrosis_factor" title="Tumor necrosis factor">\n        tumor necrosis factor\n       </a>\n       and its receptors. The role of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Wnt_signaling_pathway" title="Wnt signaling pathway">\n        Wnt signaling pathway\n       </a>\n       is recognized, but less well understood. Local production of\n       <a href="/wiki/Eicosanoid" title="Eicosanoid">\n        eicosanoids\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Interleukin" title="Interleukin">\n        interleukins\n       </a>\n       is thought to participate in the regulation of bone turnover, and excess or reduced production of these mediators may underlie the development of osteoporosis.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Raisz_26-4">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Raisz-26">\n         [26]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Trabecular_bone" title="Trabecular bone">\n        Trabecular bone\n       </a>\n       (or cancellous bone) is the sponge-like bone in the ends of long bones and vertebrae.\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cortical_bone" title="Cortical bone">\n        Cortical bone\n       </a>\n       is the hard outer shell of bones and the middle of long bones. Because osteoblasts and osteoclasts inhabit the surface of bones, trabecular bone is more active and is more subject to bone turnover and remodeling. Not only is bone density decreased, but the microarchitecture of bone is also disrupted. The weaker spicules of trabecular bone break ("microcracks"), and are replaced by weaker bone. Common osteoporotic fracture sites, the wrist, the hip and the spine, have a relatively high trabecular bone to cortical bone ratio. These areas rely on the trabecular bone for strength, so the intense remodeling causes these areas to degenerate most when the remodeling is imbalanced.\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2007)">\n           citation needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n       Around the ages of 30\xe2\x80\x9335, cancellous or trabecular bone loss begins. Women may lose as much as 50%, while men lose about 30%.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AppTher_28-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-AppTher-28">\n         [28]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Diagnosis">\n        Diagnosis\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Osteoporosis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Diagnosis">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:L1_2_vertebral_fracture.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="1747" height="326" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/L1_2_vertebral_fracture.jpg/220px-L1_2_vertebral_fracture.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/L1_2_vertebral_fracture.jpg/330px-L1_2_vertebral_fracture.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/L1_2_vertebral_fracture.jpg/440px-L1_2_vertebral_fracture.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:L1_2_vertebral_fracture.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Multiple osteoporotic wedge fractures demonstrated on a lateral thoraco-lumbar spine X-ray\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The diagnosis of osteoporosis can be made using conventional radiography and by measuring the bone mineral density (BMD).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-diagnosticimaging.com_77-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-diagnosticimaging.com-77">\n         [77]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The most popular method of measuring BMD is\n       <a href="/wiki/Dual-energy_X-ray_absorptiometry" title="Dual-energy X-ray absorptiometry">\n        dual-energy X-ray absorptiometry\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In addition to the detection of abnormal BMD, the diagnosis of osteoporosis requires investigations into potentially modifiable underlying causes; this may be done with\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Blood_tests" title="Blood tests">\n        blood tests\n       </a>\n       . Depending on the likelihood of an underlying problem, investigations for\n       <a href="/wiki/Cancer" title="Cancer">\n        cancer\n       </a>\n       with\n       <a href="/wiki/Metastasis" title="Metastasis">\n        metastasis\n       </a>\n       to the bone, multiple myeloma,\n       <a href="/wiki/Cushing%27s_disease" title="Cushing\'s disease">\n        Cushing\'s disease\n       </a>\n       and other above-mentioned causes may be performed.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Conventional_radiography">\n        Conventional radiography\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Osteoporosis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Conventional radiography">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Conventional radiography is useful, both by itself and in conjunction with CT or MRI, for detecting complications of\n       <a href="/wiki/Osteopenia" title="Osteopenia">\n        osteopenia\n       </a>\n       (reduced bone mass; pre-osteoporosis), such as fractures; for differential diagnosis of osteopenia; or for follow-up examinations in specific clinical settings, such as soft tissue calcifications, secondary hyperparathyroidism, or osteomalacia in renal osteodystrophy. However, radiography is relatively insensitive to detection of early disease and requires a substantial amount of bone loss (about 30%) to be apparent on X-ray images.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The main radiographic features of generalized osteoporosis are cortical thinning and increased radiolucency. Frequent complications of osteoporosis are vertebral fractures for which spinal radiography can help considerably in diagnosis and follow-up. Vertebral height measurements can objectively be made using plain-film X-rays by using several methods such as height loss together with area reduction, particularly when looking at vertical deformity in T4-L4, or by determining a spinal fracture index that takes into account the number of vertebrae involved. Involvement of multiple vertebral bodies leads to kyphosis of the thoracic spine, leading to what is known as\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hyperkyphosis" title="Hyperkyphosis">\n        dowager\'s hump\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Dual-energy_X-ray">\n        Dual-energy X-ray\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Osteoporosis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Dual-energy X-ray">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Dual-energy_X-ray_absorptiometry" title="Dual-energy X-ray absorptiometry">\n        Dual-energy X-ray absorptiometry\n       </a>\n       (DEXA scan) is considered the\n       <a href="/wiki/Gold_standard_(test)" title="Gold standard (test)">\n        gold standard\n       </a>\n       for the diagnosis of osteoporosis. Osteoporosis is diagnosed when the\n       <a href="/wiki/Bone_density" title="Bone density">\n        bone mineral density\n       </a>\n       is less than or equal to 2.5 standard deviations below that of a young (30\xe2\x80\x9340-year-old\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHOcriteria_4-16">\n        <a href="#cite_note-WHOcriteria-4">\n         [4]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup>\n        :58\n       </sup>\n       ), healthy adult women reference population. This is translated as a\n       <a href="/wiki/Bone_density#T-score" title="Bone density">\n        T-score\n       </a>\n       . But because bone density decreases with age, more people become osteoporotic with increasing age.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHOcriteria_4-17">\n        <a href="#cite_note-WHOcriteria-4">\n         [4]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup>\n        :58\n       </sup>\n       The World Health Organization has established the following diagnostic guidelines:\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHOcriteria_4-18">\n        <a href="#cite_note-WHOcriteria-4">\n         [4]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHO1994_19-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-WHO1994-19">\n         [19]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <table class="wikitable">\n       <tr>\n        <th>\n         Category\n        </th>\n        <th>\n         <a href="/wiki/Bone_density#T-score" title="Bone density">\n          T-score\n         </a>\n         range\n        </th>\n        <th>\n         % young women\n        </th>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         Normal\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         <a href="/wiki/Bone_density#T-score" title="Bone density">\n          T-score\n         </a>\n         \xe2\x89\xa5 \xe2\x88\x921.0\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         85%\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         <a href="/wiki/Osteopenia" title="Osteopenia">\n          Osteopenia\n         </a>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         \xe2\x88\x922.5 &lt; T-score &lt; \xe2\x88\x921.0\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         14%\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         Osteoporosis\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         T-score \xe2\x89\xa4 \xe2\x88\x922.5\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         0.6%\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         Severe osteoporosis\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         T-score \xe2\x89\xa4 \xe2\x88\x922.5 with fragility fracture\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHO1994_19-2">\n          <a href="#cite_note-WHO1994-19">\n           [19]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <p>\n       The International Society for Clinical Densitometry takes the position that a diagnosis of osteoporosis in men under 50 years of age should not be made on the basis of densitometric criteria alone. It also states, for premenopausal women, Z-scores (comparison with age group rather than peak bone mass) rather than T-scores should be used, and the diagnosis of osteoporosis in such women also should not be made on the basis of densitometric criteria alone.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pmid14742881_78-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-pmid14742881-78">\n         [78]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Biomarkers">\n        Biomarkers\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Osteoporosis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Biomarkers">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Chemical\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Biomarkers" title="Biomarkers">\n        biomarkers\n       </a>\n       are a useful tool in detecting bone degradation. The enzyme cathepsin K breaks down type-I collagen protein, an important constituent in bones. Prepared antibodies can recognize the resulting fragment, called a neoepitope, as a way to diagnose osteoporosis.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pmid15876399_79-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-pmid15876399-79">\n         [79]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Increased urinary excretion of C-telopeptides, a type-I collagen breakdown product, also serves as a biomarker for osteoporosis.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80">\n        <a href="#cite_note-80">\n         [80]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <table class="wikitable sortable">\n       <caption>\n        Comparison of bone pathology\n       </caption>\n       <tr>\n        <th>\n         <div class="plainlinks hlist navbar">\n          <ul>\n           <li class="nv-view">\n            <a href="/wiki/Template:Bone_pathology" title="Template:Bone pathology">\n             <span title="View this template">\n              view\n             </span>\n            </a>\n           </li>\n           <li class="nv-talk">\n            <a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Bone_pathology" title="Template talk:Bone pathology">\n             <span title="Discuss this template">\n              talk\n             </span>\n            </a>\n           </li>\n           <li class="nv-edit">\n            <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Bone_pathology&amp;action=edit">\n             <span title="Edit this template">\n              edit\n             </span>\n            </a>\n           </li>\n          </ul>\n         </div>\n         Condition\n        </th>\n        <th>\n         <a href="/wiki/Calcium" title="Calcium">\n          Calcium\n         </a>\n        </th>\n        <th>\n         <a href="/wiki/Phosphate" title="Phosphate">\n          Phosphate\n         </a>\n        </th>\n        <th>\n         <a href="/wiki/Alkaline_phosphatase" title="Alkaline phosphatase">\n          Alkaline phosphatase\n         </a>\n        </th>\n        <th>\n         <a href="/wiki/Parathyroid_hormone" title="Parathyroid hormone">\n          Parathyroid hormone\n         </a>\n        </th>\n        <th class="unsortable">\n         Comments\n        </th>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         <a href="/wiki/Osteopenia" title="Osteopenia">\n          Osteopenia\n         </a>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         unaffected\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         unaffected\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         normal\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         unaffected\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         decreased bone mass\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         <a href="/wiki/Osteopetrosis" title="Osteopetrosis">\n          Osteopetrosis\n         </a>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         unaffected\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         unaffected\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         elevated\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         unaffected\n         <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n          [\n          <i>\n           <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n            <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2014)">\n             citation needed\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </i>\n          ]\n         </sup>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         thick dense bones also known as marble bone\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         <a href="/wiki/Osteomalacia" title="Osteomalacia">\n          Osteomalacia\n         </a>\n         and\n         <a href="/wiki/Rickets" title="Rickets">\n          rickets\n         </a>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         decreased\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         decreased\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         elevated\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         elevated\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         soft bones\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         <a href="/wiki/Osteitis_fibrosa_cystica" title="Osteitis fibrosa cystica">\n          Osteitis fibrosa cystica\n         </a>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         elevated\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         decreased\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         elevated\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         elevated\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         brown tumors\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         <a href="/wiki/Paget%27s_disease_of_bone" title="Paget\'s disease of bone">\n          Paget\'s disease of bone\n         </a>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         unaffected\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         unaffected\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         variable (depending on stage of disease)\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         unaffected\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         abnormal bone architecture\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Other_measuring_tools">\n        Other measuring tools\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Osteoporosis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Other measuring tools">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Quantitative_computed_tomography" title="Quantitative computed tomography">\n        Quantitative computed tomography\n       </a>\n       differs from DXA in that it gives separate estimates of BMD for trabecular and cortical bone and reports precise volumetric mineral density in mg/cm\n       <sup>\n        3\n       </sup>\n       rather than BMD\'s relative Z score. Among QCT\'s advantages: it can be performed at axial and peripheral sites, can be calculated from existing CT scans without a separate radiation dose, is sensitive to change over time, can analyze a region of any size or shape, excludes irrelevant tissue such as fat, muscle, and air, and does not require knowledge of the patient\'s subpopulation in order to create a clinical score (e.g. the Z-score of all females of a certain age). Among QCT\'s disadvantages: it requires a high radiation dose compared to DXA, CT scanners are large and expensive, and because its practice has been less standardized than BMD, its results are more operator-dependent. Peripheral QCT has been introduced to improve upon the limitations of DXA and QCT.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-diagnosticimaging.com_77-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-diagnosticimaging.com-77">\n         [77]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Quantitative\n       <a href="/wiki/Ultrasound" title="Ultrasound">\n        ultrasound\n       </a>\n       has many advantages in assessing osteoporosis. The modality is small, no ionizing radiation is involved, measurements can be made quickly and easily, and the cost of the device is low compared with DXA and QCT devices. The\n       <a href="/wiki/Calcaneus" title="Calcaneus">\n        calcaneus\n       </a>\n       is the most common skeletal site for quantitative ultrasound assessment because it has a high percentage of trabecular bone that is replaced more often than cortical bone, providing early evidence of metabolic change. Also, the calcaneus is fairly flat and parallel, reducing repositioning errors. The method can be applied to children, neonates, and preterm infants, just as well as to adults.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-diagnosticimaging.com_77-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-diagnosticimaging.com-77">\n         [77]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Some ultrasound devices can be used on the\n       <a href="/wiki/Tibia" title="Tibia">\n        tibia\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81">\n        <a href="#cite_note-81">\n         [81]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Screening">\n        Screening\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Osteoporosis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Screening">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Preventive_Services_Task_Force" title="U.S. Preventive Services Task Force">\n        U.S. Preventive Services Task Force\n       </a>\n       (USPSTF) recommend that all women 65\xc2\xa0years of age or older be screened by\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bone_densitometry" title="Bone densitometry">\n        bone densitometry\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USP2011_82-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-USP2011-82">\n         [82]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Additionally they recommend screening women with increased risk factors that puts them at risk equivalent to a 65\xe2\x80\x91year\xe2\x80\x91old.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USP2011_82-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-USP2011-82">\n         [82]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       There is insufficient evidence to make recommendations about the intervals for repeated screening and the appropriate age to stop screening.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USP2011_82-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-USP2011-82">\n         [82]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In men the harm versus benefit of screening for osteoporosis is unknown.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USP2011_82-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-USP2011-82">\n         [82]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Prescrire" title="Prescrire">\n        Prescrire\n       </a>\n       states that the need to test for osteoporosis in those who have not had a previous bone fracture is unclear.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83">\n        <a href="#cite_note-83">\n         [83]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The\n       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=International_Society_for_Clinical_Densitometry&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="International Society for Clinical Densitometry (page does not exist)">\n        International Society for Clinical Densitometry\n       </a>\n       , however, suggest BMD testing for men 70 or older, or those who are indicated for risk equal to that of a 70\xe2\x80\x91year\xe2\x80\x91old.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84">\n        <a href="#cite_note-84">\n         [84]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       A number of tools exist to help determine who is reasonable to test.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pmid18716823_85-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-pmid18716823-85">\n         [85]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Prevention">\n        Prevention\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Osteoporosis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Prevention">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       Lifestyle prevention of osteoporosis is in many aspects the inverse of the potentially modifiable risk factors.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pmid25370432_86-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-pmid25370432-86">\n         [86]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       As tobacco smoking and high alcohol intake have been linked with osteoporosis, smoking cessation and moderation of alcohol intake are commonly recommended as ways to help prevent it.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Review2011_87-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Review2011-87">\n         [87]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In people with\n       <a href="/wiki/Coeliac_disease" title="Coeliac disease">\n        coeliac disease\n       </a>\n       adherence to a\n       <a href="/wiki/Gluten-free_diet" title="Gluten-free diet">\n        gluten-free diet\n       </a>\n       decreases the risk of developing osteoporosis\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LudvigssonBai2014_88-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-LudvigssonBai2014-88">\n         [88]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and increases bone density.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MirzaCanalis2015_57-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-MirzaCanalis2015-57">\n         [57]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The diet must ensure optimal\n       <a href="/wiki/Calcium" title="Calcium">\n        calcium\n       </a>\n       intake (of at least one gram daily) and measuring\n       <a href="/wiki/Vitamin_D" title="Vitamin D">\n        vitamin D\n       </a>\n       levels is recommended, and to take specific supplements if necessary.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LudvigssonBai2014_88-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-LudvigssonBai2014-88">\n         [88]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Nutrition">\n        Nutrition\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Osteoporosis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Nutrition">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Studies of the benefits of supplementation with calcium and vitamin D are conflicting, possibly because most studies did not have people with low dietary intakes.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MedicalLetter_89-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-MedicalLetter-89">\n         [89]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       A 2013 review by the USPSTF found insufficient evidence to determine if supplementation with calcium and vitamin D results in greater harm or benefit in men and premenopausal women.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USPTF2013_90-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-USPTF2013-90">\n         [90]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The USPSTF did not recommend low dose supplementation (less than 1\xc2\xa0g of calcium and 400\xc2\xa0IU of vitamin D) in postmenopausal women as there does not appear to be a difference in fracture risk.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USPTF2013_90-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-USPTF2013-90">\n         [90]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       It is unknown what effect higher doses have.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USPTF2013_90-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-USPTF2013-90">\n         [90]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       A 2015 review found little data that supplementation of calcium decreases the risk of fractures.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91">\n        <a href="#cite_note-91">\n         [91]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       While some meta-analyses have found a benefit of vitamin D supplements combined with calcium for fractures, they did not find a benefit of vitamin D supplements alone.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92">\n        <a href="#cite_note-92">\n         [92]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ave2014_93-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Ave2014-93">\n         [93]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       While supplementation does not appear to affect the risk of death,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ave2014_93-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Ave2014-93">\n         [93]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       there is an increased risk of\n       <a href="/wiki/Myocardial_infarction" title="Myocardial infarction">\n        myocardial infarctions\n       </a>\n       with calcium supplementation,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pmid20671013_94-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-pmid20671013-94">\n         [94]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pmid21505219_95-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-pmid21505219-95">\n         [95]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kidney_stones" title="Kidney stones">\n        kidney stones\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USPTF2013_90-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-USPTF2013-90">\n         [90]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and stomach problems.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ave2014_93-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Ave2014-93">\n         [93]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Vitamin_K_deficiency" title="Vitamin K deficiency">\n        Vitamin K deficiency\n       </a>\n       is also a risk factor for osteoporotic fractures. The gene\n       <a href="/wiki/Gamma-glutamyl_carboxylase" title="Gamma-glutamyl carboxylase">\n        gamma-glutamyl carboxylase (GGCX)\n       </a>\n       is dependent on vitamin K. Functional polymorphisms in the gene could attribute to variation in bone metabolism and BMD.\n       <a href="/wiki/Vitamin_K2" title="Vitamin K2">\n        Vitamin K2\n       </a>\n       is also used as a means of treatment for osteoporosis and the polymorphisms of GGCX could explain the individual variation in the response to treatment of vitamin K.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96">\n        <a href="#cite_note-96">\n         [96]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Vitamin K supplementation may reduce the risk of fractures in postmenopausal women;\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97">\n        <a href="#cite_note-97">\n         [97]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       however, there is no evidence for men.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pmid23346882_98-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-pmid23346882-98">\n         [98]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Physical_exercise">\n        Physical exercise\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Osteoporosis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Physical exercise">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       A 2011 review reported a small benefit of physical exercise on bone density of postmenopausal women.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:Howe2011_99-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-:Howe2011-99">\n         [99]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The chances of having a fracture were also slightly reduced (absolute difference 4%).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:Howe2011_99-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-:Howe2011-99">\n         [99]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       People who exercised had on average less bone loss (0.85% at the spine, 1.03% at the hip).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:Howe2011_99-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-:Howe2011-99">\n         [99]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Management">\n        Management\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Osteoporosis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Management">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Lifestyle">\n        Lifestyle\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Osteoporosis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Lifestyle">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Weight-bearing endurance exercise and/or exercises to strengthen muscles improve bone strength in those with osteoporosis.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:Howe2011_99-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-:Howe2011-99">\n         [99]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pmid21360219_100-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-pmid21360219-100">\n         [100]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Aerobics, weight bearing, and resistance exercises all maintain or increase\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bone_mineral_density" title="Bone mineral density">\n        BMD\n       </a>\n       in postmenopausal women.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:Howe2011_99-4">\n        <a href="#cite_note-:Howe2011-99">\n         [99]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Fall_prevention" title="Fall prevention">\n        Fall prevention\n       </a>\n       can help prevent osteoporosis complications. There is some evidence for\n       <a href="/wiki/Hip_protector" title="Hip protector">\n        hip protectors\n       </a>\n       specifically among those who are in care homes.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pmid21478069_101-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-pmid21478069-101">\n         [101]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Medications">\n        Medications\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Osteoporosis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Medications">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Bisphosphonate" title="Bisphosphonate">\n        Bisphosphonates\n       </a>\n       are useful in decreasing the risk of future fractures in those who have already sustained a fracture due to osteoporosis.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wells2008_5-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Wells2008-5">\n         [5]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wells2008a_6-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Wells2008a-6">\n         [6]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Review2011_87-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Review2011-87">\n         [87]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       This benefit is present when taken for three to four years.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FDA2012_102-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-FDA2012-102">\n         [102]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Different bisphosphonates have not been directly compared, therefore it is unknown if one is better than another.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Review2011_87-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Review2011-87">\n         [87]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Fracture risk reduction is between 25 and 70% depending on the bone involved.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Review2011_87-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Review2011-87">\n         [87]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       There are concerns of atypical femoral fractures and\n       <a href="/wiki/Osteonecrosis_of_the_jaw" title="Osteonecrosis of the jaw">\n        osteonecrosis of the jaw\n       </a>\n       with long-term use, but these risks are low.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Review2011_87-4">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Review2011-87">\n         [87]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103">\n        <a href="#cite_note-103">\n         [103]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       With evidence of little benefit when used for more than three to five years and in light of the potential adverse events, it may be appropriate to stop treatment after this time.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FDA2012_102-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-FDA2012-102">\n         [102]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       One medical organization recommends that after five years of medications by mouth or three years of intravenous medication among those at low risk, bisphosphonate treatment can be stopped.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ad2016_104-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Ad2016-104">\n         [104]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Qa2017_105-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Qa2017-105">\n         [105]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In those at higher risk they recommend up to ten years of medication by mouth or six years of intravenous treatment.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ad2016_104-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Ad2016-104">\n         [104]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       For those with osteoporosis but who have not had a fracture evidence does not support a reduction in fracture risk with\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Risedronate" title="Risedronate">\n        risedronate\n       </a>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wells2008a_6-4">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Wells2008a-6">\n         [6]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       or\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Etidronate" title="Etidronate">\n        etidronate\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wells2008b_9-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Wells2008b-9">\n         [9]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alendronate" title="Alendronate">\n        Alendronate\n       </a>\n       decreases\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vertebral_fractures" title="Vertebral fractures">\n        fractures of the spine\n       </a>\n       but does not have any effect on other types of fractures.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wells2008_5-4">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Wells2008-5">\n         [5]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Half stop their medications within a year.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dbt.consultantlive.com_106-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-dbt.consultantlive.com-106">\n         [106]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       When on treatment with bisphosphonates rechecking bone mineral density is not needed.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Qa2017_105-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Qa2017-105">\n         [105]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Another review found tentative evidence of benefit in males with osteoporosis.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Males2017_107-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Males2017-107">\n         [107]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Fluoride supplementation does not appear to be effective in postmenopausal osteoporosis, as even though it increases bone density, it does not decrease the risk of fractures.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108">\n        <a href="#cite_note-108">\n         [108]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109">\n        <a href="#cite_note-109">\n         [109]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Teriparatide" title="Teriparatide">\n        Teriparatide\n       </a>\n       ( a\n       <a href="/wiki/Recombinant_DNA" title="Recombinant DNA">\n        recombinant\n       </a>\n       parathyroid hormone ) has been shown to be effective in treatment of women with postmenopausal osteoporosis.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110">\n        <a href="#cite_note-110">\n         [110]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Some evidence also indicates\n       <a href="/wiki/Strontium_ranelate" title="Strontium ranelate">\n        strontium ranelate\n       </a>\n       is effective in decreasing the risk of vertebral and nonvertebral fractures in postmenopausal women with osteoporosis.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111">\n        <a href="#cite_note-111">\n         [111]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Hormone replacement therapy, while effective for osteoporosis, is only recommended in women who also have menopausal symptoms.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Review2011_87-5">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Review2011-87">\n         [87]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       It is not recommended for osteoporosis by itself.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Qa2017_105-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Qa2017-105">\n         [105]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Raloxifene" title="Raloxifene">\n        Raloxifene\n       </a>\n       , while effective in decreasing vertebral fractures, does not affect the risk of nonvertebral fracture.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Review2011_87-6">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Review2011-87">\n         [87]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       And while it reduces the risk of\n       <a href="/wiki/Breast_cancer" title="Breast cancer">\n        breast cancer\n       </a>\n       , it increases the risk of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Venous_thromboembolism" title="Venous thromboembolism">\n        blood clots\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Stroke" title="Stroke">\n        strokes\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Review2011_87-7">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Review2011-87">\n         [87]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Denosumab" title="Denosumab">\n        Denosumab\n       </a>\n       is also effective for preventing osteoporotic fractures but not in males.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Review2011_87-8">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Review2011-87">\n         [87]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Males2017_107-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Males2017-107">\n         [107]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In hypogonadal men, testosterone has been shown to improve bone quantity and quality, but, as of 2008, no studies evaluated its effect on fracture risk or in men with a normal testosterone levels.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OsteoporosisMen_56-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-OsteoporosisMen-56">\n         [56]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Calcitonin" title="Calcitonin">\n        Calcitonin\n       </a>\n       while once recommended is no longer due to the associated risk of\n       <a href="/wiki/Cancer" title="Cancer">\n        cancer\n       </a>\n       and questionable effect on fracture risk.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112">\n        <a href="#cite_note-112">\n         [112]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Certain medications like alendronate, etidronate, risedronate, raloxifene and strontium ranelate can be helpful for the preventing of osteoporotic fragility fractures in postmenopausal women with osteoporosis.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113">\n        <a href="#cite_note-113">\n         [113]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Prognosis">\n        Prognosis\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Osteoporosis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Prognosis">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <table class="wikitable" style="float:right; margin-left:15px">\n       <caption>\n        Hip fractures per 1000 person-years\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pmid17846439_114-0">\n         <a href="#cite_note-pmid17846439-114">\n          [114]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </caption>\n       <tr>\n        <th>\n         WHO category\n        </th>\n        <th>\n         Age 50\xe2\x80\x9364\n        </th>\n        <th>\n         Age &gt; 64\n        </th>\n        <th>\n         Overall\n        </th>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         Normal\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         5.3\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         9.4\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         6.6\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         <a href="/wiki/Osteopenia" title="Osteopenia">\n          Osteopenia\n         </a>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         11.4\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         19.6\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         15.7\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         Osteoporosis\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         22.4\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         46.6\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         40.6\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <p>\n       Although osteoporosis patients have an increased mortality rate due to the complications of fracture, it is rarely lethal.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Hip fractures can lead to decreased mobility and additional risks of numerous complications (such as\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Deep_venous_thrombosis" title="Deep venous thrombosis">\n        deep venous thrombosis\n       </a>\n       and/or pulmonary embolism, and\n       <a href="/wiki/Pneumonia" title="Pneumonia">\n        pneumonia\n       </a>\n       ). The six-month mortality rate for those aged 50 and above following hip fracture was found to be around 13.5%, with a substantial proportion (almost 13%) needing total assistance to mobilize after a hip fracture.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pmid11386929_115-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-pmid11386929-115">\n         [115]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Vertebral fractures, while having a smaller impact on mortality, can lead to a severe chronic pain of neurogenic origin, which can be hard to control, as well as deformity. Though rare, multiple vertebral fractures can lead to such severe hunch back (\n       <a href="/wiki/Kyphosis" title="Kyphosis">\n        kyphosis\n       </a>\n       ), the resulting pressure on internal organs can impair one\'s ability to breathe.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Apart from risk of death and other complications, osteoporotic fractures are associated with a reduced health-related\n       <a href="/wiki/Quality_of_life" title="Quality of life">\n        quality of life\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116">\n        <a href="#cite_note-116">\n         [116]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The condition is responsible for millions of fractures annually, mostly involving the lumbar vertebrae, hip, and wrist. Fragility fractures of ribs are also common in men.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Hip_fractures">\n        Hip fractures\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Osteoporosis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Hip fractures">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Hip fractures are responsible for the most serious consequences of osteoporosis. In the United States, more than 250,000 hip fractures annually are attributable to osteoporosis.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RiggsEtAl2005_117-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-RiggsEtAl2005-117">\n         [117]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       A 50-year-old white woman is estimated to have a 17.5% lifetime risk of fracture of the proximal\n       <a href="/wiki/Femur" title="Femur">\n        femur\n       </a>\n       . The incidence of hip fractures increases each decade from the sixth through the ninth for both women and men for all populations. The highest incidence is found among men and women ages 80 or older.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Merkepid_118-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Merkepid-118">\n         [118]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Vertebral_fractures">\n        Vertebral fractures\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Osteoporosis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Vertebral fractures">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Between 35 and 50% of all women over 50 had at least one\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vertebral_fracture" title="Vertebral fracture">\n        vertebral fracture\n       </a>\n       . In the United States, 700,000 vertebral fractures occur annually, but only about a third are recognized. In a series of 9704 women aged 68.8 on average studied for 15 years, 324 had already suffered a vertebral fracture at entry into the study and 18.2% developed a vertebral fracture, but that risk rose to 41.4% in women who had a previous vertebral fracture.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pmid18165669_119-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-pmid18165669-119">\n         [119]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Wrist_fractures">\n        Wrist fractures\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Osteoporosis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Wrist fractures">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       In the United States, 250,000\n       <a href="/wiki/Distal_radius_fracture" title="Distal radius fracture">\n        wrist fractures\n       </a>\n       annually are attributable to osteoporosis.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RiggsEtAl2005_117-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-RiggsEtAl2005-117">\n         [117]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Wrist fractures are the third most common type of osteoporotic fractures. The lifetime risk of sustaining a\n       <a href="/wiki/Colles%27_fracture" title="Colles\' fracture">\n        Colles\' fracture\n       </a>\n       is about 16% for white women. By the time women reach age 70, about 20% have had at least one wrist fracture.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Merkepid_118-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Merkepid-118">\n         [118]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Rib_fractures">\n        Rib fractures\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Osteoporosis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Rib fractures">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Fragility fractures of the ribs are common in men as young as age 35. These are often overlooked as signs of osteoporosis, as these men are often physically active and suffer the fracture in the course of physical activity. An example would be as a result of falling while water skiing or jet skiing. However, a quick test of the individual\'s testosterone level following the diagnosis of the fracture will readily reveal whether that individual might be at risk.\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Epidemiology">\n        Epidemiology\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Osteoporosis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Epidemiology">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       It is estimated that 200 million people have osteoporosis.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120">\n        <a href="#cite_note-120">\n         [120]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Osteoporosis becomes more common with age.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NIH2014_3-23">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NIH2014-3">\n         [3]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       About 15% of\n       <a href="/wiki/White_people" title="White people">\n        White people\n       </a>\n       in their 50s and 70% of those over 80 are affected.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHOEpi_7-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-WHOEpi-7">\n         [7]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       It is more common in women than men.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NIH2014_3-24">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NIH2014-3">\n         [3]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Developed_world" title="Developed world">\n        developed world\n       </a>\n       , depending on the method of diagnosis, 2% to 8% of males and 9% to 38% of females are affected.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wade2014_11-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Wade2014-11">\n         [11]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Rates of disease in the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Developing_world" title="Developing world">\n        developing world\n       </a>\n       are unclear.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Han2008_12-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Han2008-12">\n         [12]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       There are 8.9 million fractures worldwide per year due to osteoporosis.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-iofbonehealth.org_121-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-iofbonehealth.org-121">\n         [121]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Globally, 1 in 3 women and 1 in 5 men over the age of 50 will have an osteoporotic fracture.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-iofbonehealth.org_121-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-iofbonehealth.org-121">\n         [121]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Data from the United States shows a decrease in osteoporosis within the general population and in white women, from 18% in 1994 to 10% in 2006.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cauley_1891.E2.80.931899_122-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Cauley_1891.E2.80.931899-122">\n         [122]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       White and\n       <a href="/wiki/Asian_people" title="Asian people">\n        Asian people\n       </a>\n       are at greater risk.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NIH2014_3-25">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NIH2014-3">\n         [3]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       People of African descent are at a decreased risk of fractures due to osteoporosis, although they have the highest risk of death following an osteoporotic fracture.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cauley_1891.E2.80.931899_122-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Cauley_1891.E2.80.931899-122">\n         [122]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       It has been shown that latitude affects risk of osteoporotic fracture.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kanis_2239.E2.80.932256_123-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Kanis_2239.E2.80.932256-123">\n         [123]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Areas of higher latitude such as Northern Europe receive less Vitamin D through sunlight compared to regions closer to the equator, and consequently have higher fracture rates in comparison to lower latitudes.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kanis_2239.E2.80.932256_123-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Kanis_2239.E2.80.932256-123">\n         [123]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       For example, Swedish men and women have a 13.% and 28.5% risk of hip fracture by age 50, respectively, whereas this risk is only 1.9% and 2.4% in Chinese men and women.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cauley_1891.E2.80.931899_122-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Cauley_1891.E2.80.931899-122">\n         [122]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Diet may also be a factor that is responsible for this difference, as vitamin D, calcium, magnesium, and folate are all linked to bone mineral density.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124">\n        <a href="#cite_note-124">\n         [124]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       About 22 million women and 5.5 million men in the\n       <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">\n        European Union\n       </a>\n       had osteoporosis in 2010.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sve2013_13-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Sve2013-13">\n         [13]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In the United States in 2010 about 8 million women and one to 2 million men had osteoporosis.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wade2014_11-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Wade2014-11">\n         [11]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Will2015_14-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Will2015-14">\n         [14]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       This places a large economic burden on the healthcare system due to costs of treatment, long-term disability, and loss of productivity in the working population. The EU spends 37 billion euros per year in healthcare costs related to osteoporosis, and the USA spends an estimated 19 billion USD annually for related healthcare costs.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-iofbonehealth.org_121-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-iofbonehealth.org-121">\n         [121]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="History">\n        History\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Osteoporosis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: History">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       The link between age-related reductions in bone density and fracture risk goes back at least to\n       <a href="/wiki/Astley_Cooper" title="Astley Cooper">\n        Astley Cooper\n       </a>\n       , and the term "osteoporosis" and recognition of its pathological appearance is generally attributed to the French pathologist\n       <a href="/wiki/Jean_Lobstein" title="Jean Lobstein">\n        Jean Lobstein\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125">\n        <a href="#cite_note-125">\n         [125]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The American endocrinologist\n       <a href="/wiki/Fuller_Albright" title="Fuller Albright">\n        Fuller Albright\n       </a>\n       linked osteoporosis with the postmenopausal state.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126">\n        <a href="#cite_note-126">\n         [126]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bisphosphonates" title="Bisphosphonates">\n        Bisphosphonates\n       </a>\n       were discovered in the 1960s.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127">\n        <a href="#cite_note-127">\n         [127]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anthropologists" title="Anthropologists">\n        Anthropologists\n       </a>\n       have studied skeletal remains that showed loss of bone density and associated structural changes that were linked to a chronic malnutrition in the agricultural area in which these individuals lived. "It follows that the skeletal deformation may be attributed to their heavy labor in agriculture as well as to their chronic malnutrition", causing the osteoporosis seen when radiographs of the remains were made.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128">\n        <a href="#cite_note-128">\n         [128]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Osteoporosis means "porous bones", from Greek: \xce\xbf\xcf\x83\xcf\x84\xce\xbf\xcf\x8d\xce\xbd/\n       <i>\n        ostoun\n       </i>\n       meaning "bone" and \xcf\x80\xcf\x8c\xcf\x81\xce\xbf\xcf\x82/\n       <i>\n        poros\n       </i>\n       meaning "pore".\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="References">\n        References\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n       </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: decimal;">\n       <div August 2014.\n            <a class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20150518091922/http://www.niams.nih.gov/health_info/Osteoporosis/default.asp" rel="nofollow">\n             Archived\n            </a>\n            from the original on 18 May 2015\n            <span class="reference-accessdate">\n             . Retrieved\n             <span class="nowrap">\n              16 May\n             </span>\n             2015\n            </span>\n            .\n           </cite>\n           <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=Handout+on+Health%3A+Osteoporosis&amp;rft.date=2014-08&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.niams.nih.gov%2Fhealth_info%2FOsteoporosis%2Fdefault.asp&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AOsteoporosis">\n            <span style="display:none;">\n            </span>\n           </span>\n          </span>\n         </li>\n         <li id="cite_note-WHOcriteria-4">\n          <span class="mw-cite-backlink">\n           ^\n           <a href="#cite_ref-WHOcriteria_4-0">\n            <sup>\n             <i>\n              <b>\n               a\n              </b>\n             </i>\n            </sup>\n           </a>\n           <a href="#cite_ref-WHOcriteria_4-1">\n            <sup>\n             <i>\n              <b>\n               b\n              </b>\n             </i>\n            </sup>\n           </a>\n           <a href="#cite_ref-WHOcriteria_4-2">\n            <sup>\n             <i>\n              <b>\n               c\n              </b>\n             </i>\n            </sup>\n           </a>\n           <a href="#cite_ref-WHOcriteria_4-3">\n            <sup>\n             <i>\n              <b>\n               d\n              </b>\n
